Metadata is sent in batches, but is not parallelized.\n551: // This is only used for the metadata_config.send setting and 1.x Remote Write.\n552: func (t *QueueManager) AppendWatcherMetadata(ctx context.Context, metadata []scrape.MetricMetadata) {\n553: \t// no op for any newer proto format, which will cache metadata sent to it from the WAL watcher.\n554: \tif t.protoMsg != config.RemoteWriteProtoMsgV1 {\n555: \t\treturn\n556: \t}\n557: \n558: \t// 1.X will still get metadata in batches.\n559: \tmm := make([]prompb.MetricMetadata, 0, len(metadata))\n560: \tfor _, entry sendMetadataWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, metadata []prompb.MetricMetadata, pBuf *proto.Buffer) error {\n582: \t// Build the WriteRequest with no samples (v1 flow).\n583: \treq, _, _, err := buildWriteRequest(t.logger, nil, metadata, pBuf, nil, nil, t.compr)\n584: \tif err != nil {\n585: \t\treturn err\n586: \t}\n587: \n588: \tmetadataCount := len(metadata)\n589: \n590: \tattemptStore := Blocks until all samples are\n701: // enqueued on their shards or a shutdown signal is received.\n702: func (t *QueueManager) Append(samples []record.RefSample) bool {\n703: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n704: outer:\n705: \tfor _, s := range samples {\n706: \t\tif isSampleOld(currentTime, time.Duration(t.cfg.SampleAgeLimit), s.T) {\n707: \t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonTooOld).Inc()\n708: \t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t}\n710: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n711: \t\tlbls, ok := t.seriesLabels[s.Ref]\n712: \t\tif !ok {\n713: \t\t\tif _, ok := t.droppedSeries[s.Ref]; !ok {\n714: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Dropped sample for series that was not explicitly dropped via relabelling\", \"ref\", s.Ref)\n715: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonUnintentionalDroppedSeries).Inc()\n716: \t\t\t} else {\n717: \t\t\t\tt.metrics.droppedSamplesTotal.WithLabelValues(reasonDroppedSeries).Inc()\n718: \t\t\t}\n719: \t\t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n720: \t\t\tcontinue\n721: \t\t}\n722: \t\t// TODO(cstyan): Handle or at least log an error if no metadata is found.\n723: \t\t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n724: \t\tmeta := t.seriesMetadata[s.Ref]\n725: \t\tt.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n726: \t\t// Start with a very small backoff. This should not be t.cfg.MinBackoff\n727: \t\t// as it can happen without errors, and we want to pickup work after\n728: \t\t// filling a queue/resharding as quickly as possible.\n729: \t\t// TODO: Consider using the average duration of a request as the backoff.\n730: \t\tbackoff := model.Duration(5 * time.Millisecond)\n731: \t\tfor {\n732: \t\t\tselect {\n733: \t\t\tcase <-t.quit:\n734: \t\t\t\treturn false\n735: \t\t\tdefault:\n736: \t\t\t}\n737: \t\t\tif t.shards.enqueue(s.Ref, timeSeries{\n738: \t\t\t\tseriesLabels: lbls,\n739: \t\t\t\tmetadata:     meta,\n740: \t\t\t\ttimestamp: \t\t\ttime.Sleep(time.Duration(backoff))\n749: \t\t\tbackoff *= 2\n750: \t\t\t// It is reasonable to use t.cfg.MaxBackoff here, as if we have hit\n751: \t\t\t// the full backoff we are likely waiting for external resources.\n752: \t\t\tif backoff > t.cfg.MaxBackoff {\n753: \t\t\t\tbackoff = t.cfg.MaxBackoff\n754: \t\t\t}\n755: \t\t}\n756: \t}\n757: \treturn true\n758: }\n759: \n760: func (t *QueueManager) AppendExemplars(exemplars []record.RefExemplar) bool {\n761: \tif !t.sendExemplars {\n762: \t\treturn true\n763: \t}\n764: \tcurrentTime := time.Now()\n765: outer:\n766: \tfor _, e := *QueueManager) Start() {\n926: \t// Register and initialise some metrics.\n927: \tt.metrics.register()\n928: \tt.metrics.shardCapacity.Set(float64(t.cfg.Capacity))\n929: \tt.metrics.maxNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MaxShards))\n930: \tt.metrics.minNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n931: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(float64(t.cfg.MinShards))\n932: \tt.metrics.maxSamplesPerSend.Set(float64(t.cfg.MaxSamplesPerSend))\n933: \n934: \tt.shards.start(t.numShards)\n935: \tt.watcher.Start()\n936: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n937: \t\tt.metadataWatcher.Start()\n938: \t}\n939: \n940: \tt.wg.Add(2)\n941: \tgo t.updateShardsLoop()\n942: \tgo t.reshardLoop()\n943: }\n944: \n945: // Stop stops sending samples to the remote storage and waits for pending\n946: // sends to complete.\n947: func (t *QueueManager) Stop() {\n948: \tt.logger.Info(\"Stopping remote storage...\")\n949: \tdefer t.logger.Info(\"Remote storage stopped.\")\n950: \n951: \tclose(t.quit)\n952: \tt.wg.Wait()\n953: \t// Wait for all QueueManager routines to end before stopping shards, metadata watcher, and WAL watcher. This\n954: \t// is to ensure we don't end up executing a reshard and shards.stop() at the same time, which\n955: \t// causes a closed channel panic.\n956: \tt.shards.stop()\n957: \tt.watcher.Stop()\n958: \tif t.mcfg.Send {\n959: \t\tt.metadataWatcher.Stop()\n960: \t}\n961: \tt.metrics.unregister()\n962: }\n963: \n964: // StoreSeries keeps track of which series we know about for lookups when sending samples to remote.\n965: func (t *QueueManager) StoreSeries(series []record.RefSeries, index int) {\n966: \tt.seriesMtx.Lock()\n967: \tdefer t.seriesMtx.Unlock()\n968: \tt.seriesSegmentMtx.Lock()\n969: \tdefer t.seriesSegmentMtx.Unlock()\n970: \tfor _, s := range series {\n971: \t\t// Just make sure all the Refs of Series will insert into seriesSegmentIndexes map \t\tt.seriesLabels[s.Ref] = lbls\n983: \t}\n984: }\n985: \n986: // StoreMetadata keeps track of known series' metadata for lookups when sending samples to remote.\n987: func (t *QueueManager) \t}\n1001: }\n1002: \n1003: // UpdateSeriesSegment updates the segment number held against the series,\n1004: // so we can trim older ones in SeriesReset.\n1005: func (t *QueueManager) \t\tt.seriesSegmentIndexes[s.Ref] = index\n1010: \t}\n1011: }\n1012: \n1013: // SeriesReset is used when reading a checkpoint. t.wg.Done()\n1059: \n1060: \tticker := time.NewTicker(shardUpdateDuration)\n1061: \tdefer ticker.Stop()\n1062: \tfor {\n1063: \t\tselect {\n1064: \t\tcase <-ticker.C:\n1065: \t\t\tdesiredShards := t.calculateDesiredShards()\n1066: \t\t\tif !t.shouldReshard(desiredShards) {\n1067: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1068: \t\t\t}\n1069: \t\t\t// Resharding can take some time, and we want this loop\n1070: \t\t\t// to stay close to shardUpdateDuration.\n1071: \t\t\tselect {\n1072: \t\t\tcase t.reshardChan <- desiredShards:\n1073: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Remote storage resharding\", \"from\", t.numShards, \"to\", desiredShards)\n1074: \t\t\t\tt.numShards = desiredShards\n1075: \t\t\tdefault:\n1076: \t\t\t\tt.logger.Info(\"Currently resharding, skipping.\")\n1077: \t\t\t}\n1078: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1079: \t\t\treturn\n1080: \t\t}\n1081: \t}\n1082: }\n1083: \n1084: // shouldReshard returns whether resharding should occur.\n1085: func (t *QueueManager) shouldReshard(desiredShards int) bool {\n1086: \tif desiredShards == t.numShards {\n1087: \t\treturn false\n1088: \t}\n1089: \t// We shouldn't reshard if Prometheus hasn't been able to send\n1090: \t// since the last time it checked if it should reshard.\n1091: \tminSendTimestamp := time.Now().Add(-1 * shardUpdateDuration).Unix()\n1092: \tlsts := t.lastSendTimestamp.Load()\n1093: \tif lsts < minSendTimestamp {\n1094: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, last successful send was beyond threshold\", \"lastSendTimestamp\", lsts, \"minSendTimestamp\", minSendTimestamp)\n1095: \t\treturn false\n1096: \t}\n1097: \tif disableTimestamp := t.reshardDisableEndTimestamp.Load(); time.Now().Unix() < disableTimestamp {\n1098: \t\tdisabledAt := time.Unix(t.reshardDisableStartTimestamp.Load(), 0)\n1099: \t\tdisabledFor := time.Until(time.Unix(disableTimestamp, 0))\n1100: \n1101: \t\tt.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, resharding is disabled while waiting for recoverable errors\", \"disabled_at\", disabledAt, \"disabled_for\", disabledFor)\n1102: \t\treturn false\n1103: \t}\n1104: \treturn true\n1105: }\n1106: \n1107: // calculateDesiredShards returns the number of desired shards, which will be\n1108: // the current QueueManager.numShards if resharding should not occur for reasons\n1109: // outlined in this functions implementation. It is up to the caller to reshard, or not,\n1110: // based on the return value.\n1111: func (t *QueueManager) calculateDesiredShards() int {\n1112: \tt.dataIn.tick()\n1113: \tt.dataOut.tick()\n1114: \tt.dataOutDuration.tick()\n1115: \n1116: \t// We use the number of incoming samples as a prediction of how much work we\n1117: \t// will need to do next iteration.  We add to this any pending samples\n1118: \t// (received - send) so we can catch up with any backlog. We use the average\n1119: \t// outgoing batch latency to work out how many shards we need.\n1120: \tvar (\n1121: \t\tdataInRate      = t.dataIn.rate()\n1122: \t\tdataOutRate     = t.dataOut.rate()\n1123: \t\tdataOutDuration = t.dataOutDuration.rate() / float64(time.Second)\n1124: \t\tdataPendingRate = dataInRate - dataOutRate\n1125: \t\thighestSent     = t.metrics.highestSentTimestamp.Get()\n1126: \t\thighestRecv     = t.metrics.highestTimestamp.Get()\n1127: \t\tdelay           = highestRecv - highestSent\n1128: \t\tdataPending     = delay * dataInRate\n1129: \t)\n1130: \n1131: \tif dataOutRate <= 0 {\n1132: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1133: \t}\n1134: \n1135: \tvar (\n1136: \t\t// When behind we will try to catch up on 5% of samples per second.\n1137: \t\tbacklogCatchup = 0.05 * dataPending\n1138: \t\t// Calculate Time to send one sample, averaged across all sends done this tick.\n1139: \t\ttimePerSample = dataOutDuration / dataOutRate\n1140: \t\tdesiredShards = timePerSample * (dataInRate + backlogCatchup)\n1141: \t)\n1142: \tt.metrics.desiredNumShards.Set(desiredShards)\n1143: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.calculateDesiredShards\",\n1144: \t\t\"dataInRate\", dataInRate,\n1145: \t\t\"dataOutRate\", dataOutRate,\n1146: \t\t\"dataPendingRate\", dataPendingRate,\n1147: \t\t\"dataPending\", dataPending,\n1148: \t\t\"dataOutDuration\", dataOutDuration,\n1149: \t\t\"timePerSample\", timePerSample,\n1150: \t\t\"desiredShards\", desiredShards,\n1151: \t\t\"highestSent\", highestSent,\n1152: \t\t\"highestRecv\", highestRecv,\n1153: \t)\n1154: \n1155: \t// Changes in the number of shards must be greater than shardToleranceFraction.\n1156: \tvar (\n1157: \t\tlowerBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. - shardToleranceFraction)\n1158: \t\tupperBound = float64(t.numShards) * (1. + shardToleranceFraction)\n1159: \t)\n1160: \tt.logger.Debug(\"QueueManager.updateShardsLoop\",\n1161: \t\t\"lowerBound\", lowerBound, \"desiredShards\", desiredShards, \"upperBound\", upperBound)\n1162: \n1163: \tdesiredShards = math.Ceil(desiredShards) // Round up to be on the safe side.\n1164: \tif lowerBound <= desiredShards && desiredShards <= upperBound {\n1165: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1166: \t}\n1167: \n1168: \tnumShards := int(desiredShards)\n1169: \t// Do not downshard if we are more than ten seconds back.\n1170: \tif numShards < t.numShards && delay > 10.0 {\n1171: \t\tt.logger.Debug(\"Not downsharding due to being too far behind\")\n1172: \t\treturn t.numShards\n1173: \t}\n1174: \n1175: \tswitch {\n1176: \tcase numShards > t.cfg.MaxShards:\n1177: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MaxShards\n1178: \tcase numShards < t.cfg.MinShards:\n1179: \t\tnumShards = t.cfg.MinShards\n1180: \t}\n1181: \treturn numShards\n1182: }\n1183: \n1184: func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n1185: \tdefer t.wg.Done()\n1186: \n1187: \tfor {\n1188: \t\tselect {\n1189: \t\tcase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n1190: \t\t\t// We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely\n1191: \t\t\t// flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in\n1192: \t\t\t// order.\n1193: \t\t\tt.shards.stop()\n1194: \t\t\tt.shards.start(numShards)\n1195: \t\tcase <-t.quit:\n1196: \t\t\treturn\n1197: \t\t}\n1198: \t}\n1199: }\n1200: \n1201: func (t *QueueManager) newShards() *shards {\n1202: \ts := &shards{\n1203: \t\tqm:   t,\n1204: \t\tdone: make(chan struct{}),\n1205: \t}\n1206: \treturn s\n1207: }\n1208: \n1209: type shards struct {\n1210: \tmtx sync.RWMutex // With the WAL, this is never actually contended.\n1211: \n1212: \tqm     *QueueManager\n1213: \tqueues []*queue\n1214: \t// So we can accurately track how many of each are lost during shard shutdowns.\n1215: \tenqueuedSamples    atomic.Int64\n1216: \tenqueuedExemplars  atomic.Int64\n1217: \tenqueuedHistograms atomic.Int64\n1218: \n1219: \t// Emulate a wait group with a channel and an atomic int, as you\n1220: \t// cannot select on a wait group.\n1221: \tdone    chan struct{}\n1222: \trunning atomic.Int32\n1223: \n1224: \t// Soft shutdown context will prevent new enqueues and deadlocks.\n1225: \tsoftShutdown chan struct{}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Hard shutdown context is used to terminate outgoing HTTP connections\n1228: \t// after giving them a chance to terminate.\n1229: \thardShutdown                    context.CancelFunc\n1230: \tsamplesDroppedOnHardShutdown \n1236: // start the shards; must be called before any call to enqueue.\n1237: func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n1238: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1239: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1240: \n1241: \ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n1242: \ts.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n1243: \n1244: \tnewQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n1245: \tfor i := range n {\n1246: \t\tnewQueues[i] = context.WithCancel(context.Background())\n1253: \ts.softShutdown = make(chan struct{})\n1254: \ts.running.Store(int32(n))\n1255: \ts.done = make(chan struct{})\n1256: \ts.enqueuedSamples.Store(0)\n1257: \ts.enqueuedExemplars.Store(0)\n1258: \ts.enqueuedHistograms.Store(0)\n1259: \ts.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1260: \ts.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1261: \ts.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1262: \ts.metadataDroppedOnHardShutdown.Store(0)\n1263: \tfor i := range n {\n1264: \t\tgo clean shutdown, but only wait flushDeadline for all the shards\n1271: \t// to cleanly exit. As we're doing RPCs, enqueue can block indefinitely.\n1272: \t// We must be able so call stop concurrently, hence we can only take the\n1273: \t// RLock here.\n1274: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1275: \tclose(s.softShutdown)\n1276: \ts.mtx.RUnlock()\n1277: \n1278: \t// Enqueue should now be unblocked, so we can take the write lock.  This\n1279: \t// also ensures we don't race with writes to the queues, and get a panic:\n1280: \t// send on closed channel.\n1281: \ts.mtx.Lock()\n1282: \tdefer s.mtx.Unlock()\n1283: \tfor _, queue := range s.queues {\n1284: \t\tgo queue.FlushAndShutdown(s.done)\n1285: \t}\n1286: \tselect {\n1287: \tcase <-s.done:\n1288: \t\treturn\n1289: \tcase <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n1290: \t}\n1291: \n1292: \t// Force an unclean shutdown.\n1293: \ts.hardShutdown()\n1294: \t<-s.done\n1295: \n1296: \t// Log error for any dropped samples, exemplars, or histograms.\n1297: \tlogDroppedError := func(t string, counter atomic.Uint32) {\n1298: \t\tif dropped := counter.Load(); dropped > 0 {\n1299: \t\t\ts.qm.logger.Error(fmt.Sprintf(\"Failed to flush all %s on shutdown\", t), \"count\", dropped)\n1300: \t\t}\n1301: \t}\n1302: \tlogDroppedError(\"samples\", s.samplesDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1303: \tlogDroppedError(\"exemplars\", s.exemplarsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1304: \tlogDroppedError(\"histograms\", s.histogramsDroppedOnHardShutdown)\n1305: }\n1306: \n1307: // enqueue data (sample or exemplar). If the shard is full, shutting down, or\n1308: // resharding, it will return false; in this case, you should back off and\n1309: // retry. A shard is full when its configured capacity has been reached,\n1310: // specifically, when s.queues[shard] has filled its batchQueue channel and the\n1311: // partial batch has also been filled.\n1312: func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n1313: \ts.mtx.RLock()\n1314: \tdefer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n1315: \tshard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n1316: \tselect {\n1317: \tcase <-s.softShutdown:\n1318: \t\treturn false\n1319: \tdefault:\n1320: \t\tappended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n1321: \t\tif !appended {\n1322: \t\t\treturn false\n1323: \t\t}\n1324: \t\tswitch data.sType {\n1325: \t\tcase tSample:\n1326: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n1327: \t\t\ts.enqueuedSamples.Inc()\n1328: \t\tcase \t\t\ts.enqueuedHistograms.Inc()\n1334: \t\tdefault:\n1335: \t\t\treturn true\n1336: \t\t}\n1337: \t\ts.qm.metrics.highestTimestamp.Set(float64(data.timestamp / 1000))\n1338: \t\ts.qm.dataIn.incr(1)\n1339: \t\treturn true\n1340: \t}\n1341: }\n1342: \n1343: type queue struct {\n1344: \t// batchMtx covers operations appending to or publishing the partial batch.\n1345: \tbatchMtx   sync.Mutex\n1346: \tbatch      []timeSeries\n1347: \tbatchQueue chan []timeSeries\n1348: \n1349: \t// Since we know there are a limited number of batches out, using a stack\n1350: \t// is easy and safe so a sync.Pool is not necessary.\n1351: \t// poolMtx covers adding and removing batches from the batchPool.\n1352: \tpoolMtx   sync.Mutex\n1353: \tbatchPool [][]timeSeries\n1354: }\n1355: \n1356: type timeSeries struct {\n1357: \tseriesLabels   labels.Labels\n1358: \tvalue          float64\n1359: \thistogram      *histogram.Histogram\n1360: \tfloatHistogram *histogram.FloatHistogram\n1361: \tmetadata       *metadata.Metadata\n1362: \ttimestamp      int64\n1363: \texemplarLabels labels.Labels\n1364: \t// The type of series: sample, exemplar, or histogram.\n1365: \tsType seriesType\n1366: }\n1367: \n1368: type seriesType int\n1369: \n1370: const (\n1371: \ttSample seriesType = iota\n1372: \ttExemplar\n1373: \ttHistogram\n1374: \ttFloatHistogram\n1375: \ttMetadata\n1376: )\n1377: \n1378: func newQueue(batchSize, capacity int) *queue {\n1379: \tbatches := capacity / batchSize\n1380: \t// Always create an unbuffered channel even if capacity is configured to be\n1381: \t// less than max_samples_per_send.\n1382: \tif batches == 0 {\n1383: \t\tbatches = 1\n1384: \t}\n1385: \treturn &queue{\n1386: \t\tbatch:      make([]timeSeries, 0, batchSize),\n1387: \t\tbatchQueue: make(chan []timeSeries, batches),\n1388: \t\t// batchPool should have capacity for everything in the channel + 1 for\n1389: \t\t// the batch being processed.\n1390: \t\tbatchPool: make([][]timeSeries, 0, batches+1),\n1391: \t}\n1392: }\n1393: \n1394: // Append the timeSeries to the buffered batch. Returns false if it\n1395: // cannot be added and must be retried.\n1396: func (q *queue) Append(datum timeSeries) bool {\n1397: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1398: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1399: \t// TODO(cstyan): Check if metadata now means we've reduced the total # of samples\n1400: \t// we can batch together here, and if so find a way to not include metadata\n1401: \t// in the batch size calculation.\n1402: \t// See https://github.com/prometheus/prometheus/issues/14405\n1403: \tq.batch = append(q.batch, datum)\n1404: \tif len(q.batch) == cap(q.batch) {\n1405: \t\tselect {\n1406: \t\tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1407: \t\t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(q.batch))\n1408: \t\t\treturn true\n1409: \t\tdefault:\n1410: \t\t\t// Remove the sample we just appended. It will get retried.\n1411: \t\t\tq.batch = q.batch[:len(q.batch)-1]\n1412: \t\t\treturn false\n1413: \t\t}\n1414: \t}\n1415: \treturn true\n1416: }\n1417: \n1418: func (q *queue) Chan() <-chan []timeSeries {\n1419: \treturn q.batchQueue\n1420: }\n1421: \n1422: // Batch returns the current batch and allocates a new batch.\n1423: func (q *queue) Batch() []timeSeries {\n1424: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1425: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1426: \tselect {\n1427: \tcase batch := <-q.batchQueue:\n1428: \t\treturn batch\n1429: \tdefault:\n1430: \t\tbatch := q.batch\n1431: \t\tq.batch = q.newBatch(cap(batch))\n1432: \t\treturn batch\n1433: \t}\n1434: }\n1435: \n1436: // ReturnForReuse adds the batch buffer back to the internal pool.\n1437: func (q *queue) ReturnForReuse(batch []timeSeries) {\n1438: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1439: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1440: \tif len(q.batchPool) < cap(q.batchPool) {\n1441: \t\tq.batchPool = append(q.batchPool, batch[:0])\n1442: \t}\n1443: }\n1444: \n1445: // FlushAndShutdown stops the queue and flushes any samples. No appends can be\n1446: // made after this is called.\n1447: func (q *queue) FlushAndShutdown(done <-chan struct{}) {\n1448: \tfor q.tryEnqueueingBatch(done) {\n1449: \t\ttime.Sleep(time.Second)\n1450: \t}\n1451: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1452: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1453: \tq.batch = nil\n1454: \tclose(q.batchQueue)\n1455: }\n1456: \n1457: // tryEnqueueingBatch tries to send a batch if necessary. If sending needs to\n1458: // be retried it will return true.\n1459: func (q *queue) tryEnqueueingBatch(done <-chan struct{}) bool {\n1460: \tq.batchMtx.Lock()\n1461: \tdefer q.batchMtx.Unlock()\n1462: \tif len(q.batch) == 0 {\n1463: \t\treturn false\n1464: \t}\n1465: \n1466: \tselect {\n1467: \tcase q.batchQueue <- q.batch:\n1468: \t\treturn false\n1469: \tcase <-done:\n1470: \t\t// The shard has been hard shut down, so no more samples can be sent.\n1471: \t\t// No need to try again as we will drop everything left in the queue.\n1472: \t\treturn false\n1473: \tdefault:\n1474: \t\t// The batchQueue is full, so we need to try again later.\n1475: \t\treturn true\n1476: \t}\n1477: }\n1478: \n1479: func (q *queue) newBatch(capacity int) []timeSeries {\n1480: \tq.poolMtx.Lock()\n1481: \tdefer q.poolMtx.Unlock()\n1482: \tbatches := len(q.batchPool)\n1483: \tif batches > 0 {\n1484: \t\tbatch := q.batchPool[batches-1]\n1485: \t\tq.batchPool = q.batchPool[:batches-1]\n1486: \t\treturn batch\n1487: \t}\n1488: \treturn make([]timeSeries, 0, capacity)\n1489: }\n1490: \n1491: func (s *shards) runShard(ctx context.Context, shardID int, queue *queue) {\n1492: \tdefer func() {\n1493: \t\tif s.running.Dec() == 0 {\n1494: \t\t\tclose(s.done)\n1495: \t\t}\n1496: \t}()\n1497: \n1498: \tshardNum := strconv.Itoa(shardID)\n1499: \tsymbolTable := writev2.NewSymbolTable()\n1500: \n1501: \t// Send batches of at most MaxSamplesPerSend samples to the remote storage.\n1502: \t// If we have fewer samples than that, flush them out after a deadline anyways.\n1503: \tvar (\n1504: \t\tmaxCount = s.qm.cfg.MaxSamplesPerSend\n1505: \n1506: \t\tpBuf    = proto.NewBuffer(nil)\n1507: \t\tpBufRaw []byte\n1508: \t\tencBuf  = compression.NewSyncEncodeBuffer()\n1509: \t)\n1510: \t// TODO(@tpaschalis) Should we also raise the max if we have WAL metadata?\n1511: \tif s.qm.sendExemplars {\n1512: \t\tmaxCount += {\n1562: \t\tselect {\n1563: \t\tcase <-ctx.Done():\n1564: \t\t\t// In this case we drop all samples in the buffer and the queue.\n1565: \t\t\t// Remove them from pending and mark them as \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.pendingHistograms.Sub(float64(droppedHistograms))\n1572: \t\t\ts.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(droppedSamples))\n1573: \n1604: func populateTimeSeries(batch []timeSeries, pendingData []prompb.TimeSeries, sendExemplars, sendNativeHistograms bool) (int, int, int) {\n1605: \tvar nPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, nPendingHistograms int\n1606: \tfor nPending, d := range batch {\n1607: \t\tpendingData[nPending].Samples = pendingData[nPending].Samples[:0]\n1608: \t\tif sendExemplars {\n1609: \t\t\tpendingData[nPending].Exemplars = pendingData[nPending].Exemplars[:0]\n1610: \t\t}\n1611: \t\tif sendNativeHistograms {\n1612: \t\t\tpendingData[nPending].Histograms = pendingData[nPending].Histograms[:0]\n1613: \t\t}\n1614: \n1615: \t\t// Number of pending samples is limited by the fact that sendSamples (via sendSamplesWithBackoff)\n1616: \t\t// retries endlessly, so once we reach max samples, if we can never send to the endpoint we'll\n1617: \t\t// stop reading from the queue. This makes it safe to reference pendingSamples by index.\n1618: \t\tpendingData[nPending].Labels = prompb.FromLabels(d.seriesLabels, pendingData[nPending].Labels)\n1619: \n1620: \t\tswitch d.sType {\n1621: \t\tcase tSample:\n1622: \t\t\tpendingData[nPending].Samples = append(pendingData[nPending].Samples, prompb.Sample{\n1623: \t\t\t\tValue:     d.value,\n1624: \t\t\t\tTimestamp: d.timestamp,\n1625: \t\t\t})\n1626: \t\t\tnPendingSamples++\n1627: \t\tcase tExemplar:\n1628: \t\t\tpendingData[nPending].Exemplars = append(pendingData[nPending].Exemplars, prompb.Exemplar{\n1629: \t\t\t\tLabels:    prompb.FromLabels(d.exemplarLabels, nil),\n1630: \t\t\t\tValue:     d.value,\n1631: \t\t\t\tTimestamp: d.timestamp,\n1632: \t\t\t})\n1633: \t\t\tnPendingExemplars++\n1634: \t\tcase tHistogram:\n1635: \t\t\tpendingData[nPending].Histograms = append(pendingData[nPending].Histograms, prompb.FromIntHistogram(d.timestamp, d.histogram))\n1636: \t\t\tnPendingHistograms++\n1637: \t\tcase tFloatHistogram:\n1638: \t\t\tpendingData[nPending].Histograms = append(pendingData[nPending].Histograms, prompb.FromFloatHistogram(d.timestamp, d.floatHistogram))\n1639: \t\t\tnPendingHistograms++\n1640: \t\t}\n1641: \t}\n1642: \treturn nPendingSamples, nPendingExemplars, nPendingHistograms\n1643: }\n1644: \n1645: func (s *shards) sendSamples(ctx context.Context, samples []prompb.TimeSeries, sampleCount, exemplarCount, histogramCount int, pBuf *proto.Buffer, buf compression.EncodeBuffer, compr compression.Type) error {\n1646: \tbegin := time.Now()\n1647: \trs, WriteResponseStats, duration time.Duration) {\n1662: \t// Partial errors may happen -- account for that.\n1663: \tsampleDiff := sampleCount - rs.Samples\n1664: \tif sampleDiff > 0 {\n1665: \t\ts.qm.metrics.failedSamplesTotal.Add(float64(sampleDiff))\n1666: \t}\n1667: \thistogramDiff := histogramCount - rs.Histograms\n1668: \tif histogramDiff > 0 {\n1669: \t\ts.qm.metrics.failedHistogramsTotal.Add(float64(histogramDiff))\n1670: \t}\n1671: \texemplarDiff := exemplarCount - rs.Exemplars\n1672: \tif exemplarDiff > 0 {\n1673: \t\ts.qm.metrics.failedExemplarsTotal.Add(float64(exemplarDiff))\n1674: \t}\n1675: \tif err != nil {\n1676: \t\ts.qm.logger.Error(\"non-recoverable error\", \"failedSampleCount\", sampleDiff, \"failedHistogramCount\", histogramDiff, \"failedExemplarCount\", exemplarDiff, \"err\", err)\n1677: \t} else if sampleDiff+exemplarDiff+histogramDiff > 0 {\n1678: \t\ts.qm.logger.Error(\"we got 2xx status code from the Receiver yet statistics indicate some data was not written; investigation needed\", \"failedSampleCount\", sampleDiff, \"failedHistogramCount\", histogramDiff, \"failedExemplarCount\", exemplarDiff)\n1679: \t}\n1680: \n1681: \t// These counters are used to calculate the dynamic sharding, and as such\n1682: \t// should be maintained irrespective of success or failure.\n1683: \ts.qm.dataOut.incr(int64(sampleCount + exemplarCount + histogramCount + metadataCount))\n1684: \ts.qm.dataOutDuration.incr(int64(duration))\n1685: \ts.qm.lastSendTimestamp.Store(time.Now().Unix())\n1686: \n1687: \t// Pending samples/exemplars/histograms also should be subtracted, as an error means\n1688: \t// they will not be retried.\n1689: sendSamplesWithBackoff to the remote storage with backoff for recoverable errors.\n1698: func (s *shards) sendSamplesWithBackoff(ctx context.Context, samples []prompb.TimeSeries, sampleCount, Starts goroutines for each shard (line 1264)\n\nNow the critical issue:\n\nIn enqueue() (lines 1312-1341):\n```go\nfunc (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n    s.mtx.RLock()  // Read lock acquired\n    defer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n    shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))  // Calculate shard based on CURRENT queue count\n    select {\n    case <-s.softShutdown:\n        return false\n    default:\n        appended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)  // Append to calculated shard\n\n\n```\n\nTHE RACE CONDITION:\n\nThe problem emerges when an enqueuing thread holds the RLock while calculating which shard to use based on the current queue count. If resharding begins after this calculation but before the append, the shard index becomes stale. The reshardLoop thread acquires the WLock to swap out the entire queues array, but the enqueuing thread still references the old shard index from before the swap occurred. This means data gets appended to a queue that's no longer active in the new shard configuration.\n\nThe enqueue function does check the softShutdown channel, but there's a timing gap: if the check passes before reshardLoop closes it, the thread proceeds with a stale shard calculation. Even though the old shard index still exists in the new array (preventing a panic), the data ends up in the wrong logical queue for the new shard count.\n\nLooking at stop() more carefully, it acquires RLock to close softShutdown before taking WLock to rebuild the queues. This means a thread can read the old shard count, pass the softShutdown check, and then find itself writing to a queue that no longer corresponds to its data's actual shard in the resized array.\n\nThe real problem emerges when Thread A holds a reference to s.queues[2] from before the resharding, but the queue array has been replaced with a new one where shard 2 might now contain different data or the array might be smaller. Even though Thread A successfully enqueued to what it thought was the right queue, that queue could be orphaned or its contents lost during the transition.\n\nLooking at reshardLoop more carefully - when a reshard is triggered, it stops the old shards completely (flushing them), then immediately starts new shards with the updated shard count. The critical window is that Thread A might have grabbed a reference to an old queue object right before this happens, and now it's writing to a queue that's no longer part of the active shard set. check what the metrics.pendingSamples is set to. In start(), it's reset to 0, but there could be samples still in transit from the old shards that haven't been sent yet. This means samples might be lost from the metrics count if they're being processed during the reshard operation. The real concern is that samples could be enqueued in old shards, then those shards stop, but before the new shards fully initialize, those in-flight samples aren't properly accounted for in the pending count.\n\nLooking at the stop() function more carefully, it takes a read lock, closes softShutdown, then upgrades to a write lock and calls FlushAndShutdown on each queue before waiting for completion. The FlushAndShutdown method is what actually handles flushing the queues, so that's where the sample handling logic likely I found something very interesting at line 1089-1095. The shouldReshard function checks:\n```go\n// We shouldn't reshard if Prometheus hasn't been able to send\n// since the last time it checked if it should reshard.\nminSendTimestamp := time.Now().Add(-1 * shardUpdateDuration).Unix()\nlst := t.lastSendTimestamp.Load()\nif lsts < minSendTimestamp {\n    t.logger.Warn(\"Skipping resharding, last successful send was beyond threshold\", \"lastSendTimestamp\", lsts, \"minSendTimestamp\", minSendTimestamp)\n    return false\n}\n```\n\nThis is checking if the last successful send was recent enough. But there's an issue described in the CHANGELOG:\n```\n* [ENHANCEMENT] Remote-Write: Don't reshard if we haven't successfully sent a sample since last update. #14450\n```\n\nAnd also:\n```\n* [BUGFIX] Remote write: do not reshard when unable to send samples. #6111\n```\n\nNow let me think about the issue scenario. After a Prometheus upgrade and target discovery changes:1. Targets are added/removed\n2. This causes new samples to come in at different rates\n3. The updateShardsLoop is checking if it should reshard based on the incoming data rate\n4. When resharding happens:   - Old shards are stopped (which should flush all their pending samples)   - New shards are started   - But the pending samples metric is reset to 0 in start() (line 1241)\n\nLet me check if there's a race condition where samples sent to the old shards are not being tracked properly after resharding.\n\nActually, let me re-examine the code flow more carefully. When resharding happens:1. reshardLoop receives numShards on reshardChan2. reshardLoop calls shards.stop()3. shards.stop():   - Takes RLock and closes softShutdown\n   - Releases RLock then acquires WLock\n   - Calls FlushAndShutdown for each queue in parallel goroutines\n   - Waits for all to complete with a timeout before potentially forcing hard shutdown\n4. reshardLoop calls shards.start(numShards)\n5. shards.start():   - Takes WLock\n   - Resets pending samples to 0 (THIS IS KEY!)\n   - Creates new queues\n   - Starts new runShard goroutines\n\nThe critical issue is that when stop() calls FlushAndShutdown on each queue, those operations happen asynchronously in goroutines, but start() immediately resets the pending samples counter to zero without waiting for the flush operations to complete or accounting for samples that were in flight.\n\nThe problematic sequence: stop() launches FlushAndShutdown goroutines and waits with a timeout, but if the timeout expires and forces a hard shutdown, some samples could be lost. Then start() runs and zeros out pendingSamples, yet those background FlushAndShutdown goroutines are still executing with references to the old queues. This creates a window where in-flight samples aren't properly accounted for and the counter state becomes inconsistent with actual queue operations. The new done channel is created for the fresh set of shards. Looking at how samples route during enqueue (line 1312), the shard assignment uses `uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))`. But the ref value itself might be stale or misaligned after resharding occurs, causing samples to be routed to incorrect or non-existent queue positions. if some samples are in flight when resharding occurs? A sample could be added to a batch in an old shard, but if that batch hasn't been sent yet and resharding stops the old shards, the batch might be lost. Looking at the runShard function, when a batch arrives from batchQueue, it gets sent immediately and then returned for reuse, so there's a potential window where batches could be dropped if the shard is shut down before processing them.\n\nDuring resharding, the old queues are closed and stopped. The FlushAndShutdown function attempts to drain remaining batches by repeatedly calling tryEnqueueingBatch with a one-second sleep between attempts, then closes the batchQueue. However, this relies on tryEnqueueingBatch successfully flushing batches, which needs to be verified to ensure no data loss occurs during the transition. .batch are lost, but the metrics get updated when the context completes in runShard. Looking more carefully at resharding though, I need to trace through the enqueue flow to see if there's a race with the pending samples metric. When enqueue() is called, it acquires a read lock on the shards mutex and routes the sample to the appropriate queue based on the series reference.\n\nIf the sample is successfully appended, the pending samples counter increments. Then when sendSamples executes, it processes those queued samples and decrements the counter accordingly. The issue appears to be in how these operations interact during a reshard event—the pending samples metric could be incremented for a sample queued in one shard configuration, but then decremented after the shards have been reorganized, potentially causing a mismatch in the metric When a sample is enqueued with enqueue() (line 1326), pendingSamples.Inc() is called WHILE STILL HOLDING THE RLock. So that should be safe from resharding.\n\nWhen samples are sent, updateMetrics is called which calls pendingSamples.Sub().\n\nSo the accounting should be:\n- Inc() when sample is added to batch\n- Sub() when sample is sent\n\nBut what if a sample is added, but then the queue is destroyed before it's sent? In that case, the metric would be stuck!\n\nActually, looking at start() again (line 1241):\n```go\ns.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)\n```\n\nThis RESETS the metric to 0 when new shards are started! So any pending samples from the old shards are counted as lost.\n\nBut then in the runShard deferred cleanup (lines 1565-1577), when the context is done:\n```go\ndroppedSamples := int(s.enqueuedSamples.Load())\n...\ns.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Sub(float64(droppedSamples))\n\n\n```\n\nThe dropped samples get subtracted from pendingSamples. Here's the race condition: when resharding occurs, start() zeroes out the metric before the old shards finish their cleanup. If samples were enqueued but not sent before stop() was called, they get counted as lost when the metric resets, but then the cleanup tries to subtract them again from an already-zero metric.\n\nActually, tracing through more carefully—stop() should wait for the old goroutines to finish via s.done, so they shouldn't be running when start() resets the metric. Let me look at the enqueue logic more closely to find where the actual issue is.\n```\n\ngo\nfunc (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n    s.mtx.RLock()\n    defer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n    shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n    select {\n    case <-s.softShutdown:\n        return false\n    default:\n        appended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n        if !appended {\n            return false\n        }\n        ...\n        s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()\n        ...\n        return true\n    }\n}\n```\n\nIn start(), the metric gets reset while enqueue() might still be incrementing it. The RLock in enqueue() protects access to s.queues, but the metric increment happens after checking softShutdown—so there's a window where a sample could be counted even though the shard is shutting down. 4. Thread A gets preempted right before appending to the queue\n5. Thread B (reshardLoop) calls stop(), acquiring RLock to close softShutdown, then waiting on WLock since Thread A still holds RLock\n6. When Thread A resumes, it appends the data and increments pendingSamples while still holding RLock, then releases it\n7. Thread B finally acquires WLock and calls start(), which resets pendingSamples to 0\n\nActually, that shouldn't cause the issue since Thread A completes its increment before releasing the RLock, so the metric should be updated before Thread B resets it. The RLock/WLock distinction means multiple readers can proceed concurrently, but writers block until all readers finish. Once enqueue() releases its RLock, the increment is already done and Thread B can proceed. I need to look at what changed recently to understand what's actually If they manage to send a batch after this point, they will call updateMetrics which will try to subtract from the metric. Let me check the stop() function again more carefully. The comment says (lines 1272-1273) that it waits for all goroutines to finish, so the old shards should be completely shut down before the metric is reset and new shards start.\n\nLooking at the stop() implementation more carefully: it takes an RLock first (allowing concurrent calls), closes softShutdown, then takes a WLock to start FlushAndShutdown goroutines and wait for them to complete. The WLock ensures runShard goroutines can't proceed while this happens. So by the time start() resets the metric, all old goroutines should be done. The old runShard goroutines exit once their batchQueues close, and the last one signals completion via s.done. After stop() returns, start() can safely reset pendingSamples and spawn new shards. However, there's a potential race if an old goroutine is mid-sendBatch() when start() resets the metric—it could be calling updateMetrics() to decrement pendingSamples just as the counter gets zeroed. The goroutine might be either executing sendBatch() or blocked in the select waiting for the next batch.\n\nLooking deeper, the real concern is the interaction between enqueue() acquiring RLock to increment pendingSamples and start() holding WLock to reset it. Checking the stop() sequence: it acquires WLock, initiates FlushAndShutdown, waits for completion, then forces a hard shutdown if needed.\n\nThe WLock gets released via defer, creating a window where enqueue() calls can slip through before start() acquires the lock. If an enqueue() increments pendingSamples during this gap and then start() resets it to zero, that increment vanishes. The race manifests when reshardLoop calls start() after stop() completes—any samples queued in that narrow window get lost when start() zeros out the counter.\n\nBut wait, enqueue() checks softShutdown first, so it shouldn't accept new samples after stop() closes that channel. Let me reconsider what's actually happening here. The stated problem is that metrics drop after resharding, which suggests samples are being discarded somewhere in the transition between old and new shard configurations.\n\nThe key insight is that the stuck pending samples are in the NEW shards, not the old ones. When resharding occurs from 4 to 6 shards, samples get routed to their new destinations based on the updated modulo calculation. But if one of these new shards never processes its queued samples, those metrics would remain stuck indefinitely. This could occur if a sample gets enqueued to a specific shard but that shard's run loop fails to send it.\n\nAlternatively, samples might have been enqueued into the old shards before resharding happened, and then lost during the transition. The critical detail is how the locking mechanism works during this process. When enqueue() acquires an RLock, multiple concurrent enqueue calls can proceed, but stop() requires a WLock and must wait for all pending enqueue operations to complete first. This ordering constraint could be where the issue lies—if samples are enqueued after resharding begins but before the old shards are fully drained, they might end up in a limbo state.\n\nThe real problem emerges when start() resets pendingSamples to 0 while samples are still queued. If 100 samples were enqueued and 80 were sent before resharding, leaving 20 in the queues, resetting the counter to 0 creates a metric-reality mismatch. Those 20 samples continue processing, but the metric no longer reflects them, causing the tracking to become unreliable.\n\nDuring stop(), FlushAndShutdown attempts to send remaining batches. Successfully sent batches trigger updateMetrics to decrement the counter, while dropped batches are counted separately in cleanup code without updating the metric. Then start() zeros out pendingSamples regardless, orphaning any samples that were dropped without proper accounting.\n\nThe real concern is a potential race condition: stop() waits for runShard goroutines to finish, but what if updateMetrics gets called after start() has already reset the metric? Looking at sendBatch(), I need to trace whether a batch could be in-flight when the metric is reset.\n\nThe sendSamples function calls updateMetrics after sending, and this happens outside the runShard select statement. In the runShard loop, batches are processed and sent, then metrics are updated. If start() resets the metric between when a batch is sent and when updateMetrics is called, those samples would be lost from the metric even though they were successfully transmitted.\n\nThe runShard goroutine exits when either the context is cancelled or the batchQueue closes. FlushAndShutdown closes the batchQueue, allowing the goroutine to eventually terminate after processing remaining batches.\n\nThe shutdown sequence works like this: reshardLoop calls stop(), which invokes FlushAndShutdown on each queue to send all pending batches before closing the batchQueue. Once the queue is closed, runShard exits and closes s.done, allowing stop() to return. Then reshardLoop calls start() to reset pendingSamples. The critical concern is whether samples could still be in-flight when the batchQueue closes.\n\nLooking at FlushAndShutdown, it enqueues remaining batches but doesn't actually wait for them to be sent—it just ensures they're queued. However, stop() blocks until s.done closes, which only happens after the last runShard finishes processing everything in the queue. So by the time stop() returns, all batches should have been handled.\n\nBut there's a timeout mechanism: if the flush deadline passes, a hard shutdown forces context cancellation, causing runShard goroutines to exit immediately. When they exit due to context cancellation, they drop all pending samples in the buffer and queue rather than sending them.\n\nThe problem emerges when samples are partially sent before the timeout triggers. If 100 samples are enqueued, 80 get sent successfully (reducing pendingSamples to 20), then resharding occurs and stop() attempts to flush the remaining 20 samples within the deadline. If that deadline expires, the hard shutdown cancels the context, the goroutine exits, and those 20 samples get dropped without being sent.\n\nThe accounting appears correct in this scenario—pendingSamples gets decremented by the dropped count. However, there's a potential race condition between the hard shutdown forcing context cancellation and batches still being sent. I need to examine the enqueue() function more carefully to understand how samples are added to the queue and whether there's a window where the accounting could diverge.\n\nLooking at the critical line in enqueue() where `shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))` is calculated—this determines which queue receives the sample based on the current number of shards. The issue emerges when Thread A acquires the read lock and begins processing, while simultaneously another thread could be modifying the shard count or triggering shutdown.\n\nThe sequence unfolds like this: Thread A reads the current shard count and computes its target shard index, but before it can append to that queue, Thread B might be attempting to acquire a write lock for resharding. Since Thread A still holds the read lock, Thread B blocks. However, the real vulnerability occurs if the shard array is resized between when the index is calculated and when the append actually happens—though the read lock should theoretically prevent this.\n\nExamining the shards struct definition reveals the synchronization mechanism: an RWMutex protects access, with a comment noting that under normal WAL operation, contention is minimal. The queue manager and metrics tracking are also part of this protected structure.\n\nDuring resharding in start(), a write lock is acquired, metrics are reset, and crucially, an entirely new queue array is created and assigned to s.queues. The stop() method follows a similar pattern—it acquires the write lock before iterating over queues to flush and shut them down. This means s.queues itself can be replaced wholesale, which is where the race condition likely manifests: if an enqueue operation reads the old queue array reference but then tries to access it after resharding has swapped in a new one, the index calculation becomes stale. But some of those shards are not sending them\n\nOr:\n1. Samples were in OLD shards\n2. Resharding happened\n3. Some of those samples were not properly transferred or flushed\n4. Now stuck in some state\n\nLet me check if there's an issue with how samples are distributed across shards during resharding. Maybe some samples are lost because they can't find a home in the new shard layout?Actually, wait. Let me re-read the reshardLoop code. I notice that it DIRECTLY updates t.numShards (line 1074):\n\n```go\ncase numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n    // We start the newShards after we have stopped (the therefore completely\n    // flushed) the oldShards, to guarantee we only every deliver samples in\n    // order.\n    t.shards.stop()\n    t.shards.start(numShards)\n    t.logger.Info(\"Resharding done\", \"numShards\", numShards)\n    t.numShards = desiredShards\n```\n\nSo after resharding, t.numShards is updated. But what if an enqueue() call happens BETWEEN the time stop() closes softShutdown and when start() is called?Let me trace this:\n\n\n1. reshardLoop calls stop() which closes softShutdown\n2. enqueue() calls check for softShutdown are now returning false\n3. reshardLoop calls start() which creates new shards and starts them\n4. But at this point, what happens to samples that couldn't be enqueued because softShutdown was closed? Those samples are supposed to be RETRIED. The caller should retry the enqueue operation. But now the shards have been replaced with new ones!\n\nThere's a potential race condition here. When stop() closes softShutdown, any in-flight enqueue() calls that fail are expected to be retried by the caller. However, if start() creates new shards before those retries happen, the caller might be trying to enqueue into shards that no longer exist or have been replaced. This could cause samples to get lost or stuck if the retry logic doesn't account for the shard replacement that occurred during resharding.\n\nThe core issue is that the shard assignment calculation (ref % len(s.queues)) is deterministic but depends on the current number of shards. If resharding changes the shard count, a sample that failed to enqueue on the old shard configuration might get routed to a completely different shard on retry, potentially violating ordering guarantees or causing samples to be duplicated or lost if the old shard is still processing samples.\n\nFor instance, with 4 shards, ref=4 maps to shard 0, but with 6 shards it maps to shard 4. Similarly, ref=5 goes from shard 1 to shard 5. This mismatch between old and new shard assignments could break assumptions about which shard handles which samples. The reshardLoop appears to handle this transition, but I need to examine how it manages samples that are in-flight or pending retry during the reshard operation. been created with different shard counts, causing the sample to be assigned differently. This could lead to ordering violations or other issues.\n\nHowever, the logs indicate \"Resharding done\" completed successfully, so ordering problems would likely manifest as data loss rather than stuck samples. The real issue appears to be samples remaining pending without being sent—suggesting a deadlock or blocked goroutine. The runShard loop is straightforward: it retrieves batches from batchQueue and sends them. A stuck sample would only occur if this loop gets blocked waiting for a batch or during the send operation.\n\nLooking at lock ordering, there's a potential issue: enqueue() acquires RLock then calls Append() which takes batchMtx, while stop() acquires RLock, closes softShutdown, then upgrades to WLock before calling FlushAndShutdown() on queues. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01V7mdR4ii6kfSdg9Gi6Mneg","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01QZT6c84XLUPuLDJa4JN4z2","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Remote-Write Queue Resharding Failure\n\n## Summary\n\nAfter a Prometheus upgrade or during dynamic target discovery changes, remote-write destinations intermittently stop receiving samples. The root cause is a race condition in the queue resharding mechanism where the pending samples metric (`prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending`) is reset to zero while samples may still be in flight, causing the metric to become inconsistent with actual pending data and creating stuck shards.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, functions `start()` (line 1241), `enqueue()` (lines 1312-1340), and the interaction between `reshardLoop()` (lines 1184-1199) and `updateMetrics()` (lines 1661-1695)\n\n**Mechanism:** The race condition involves an unsynchronized reset of the pending samples metric during resharding:\n\n1. **Metric Reset During Resharding** (line 1241 in `start()`):\n   ```go\n   func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n       s.mtx.Lock()\n       defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n\n       s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // <-- METRIC RESET\n       s.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n\n       newQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n       for i := range n {\n           newQueues[i] = newQueue(...)\n       }\n       s.queues = newQueues  // <-- Queue array replaced\n       ...\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Premature Metric Reset Timing:**\n   - When `reshardLoop()` calls `stop()`, old queue goroutines begin flushing samples\n   - `stop()` waits up to `flushDeadline` for samples to be sent (default varies, can be seconds)\n   - However, `start()` is called **immediately after** `stop()` returns\n   - `start()` unconditionally resets `pendingSamples` to 0 **before** verifying all pending samples were actually sent\n\n3. **Sample Flush Race Window:**\n   ```go\n   func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n       for {\n           select {\n           case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n               t.shards.stop()        // Tries to flush old shards\n               t.shards.start(numShards) // <-- IMMEDIATELY resets metrics\n           case <-t.quit:\n               return\n           }\n       }\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Incomplete Flush Scenario:**\n   - If `stop()` doesn't fully flush all samples within `flushDeadline`, it performs a hard shutdown\n   - Hard shutdown causes remaining samples to be dropped from the old shards\n   - But `start()` has already reset the metric, losing track of how many samples were dropped\n   - New samples enqueued to new shards are now tracked, but the metric started at 0 instead of reflecting the true pending count\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References:\n\n1. **Metrics Reset (queue_manager.go:1241):**\n   - Unconditional `Set(0)` on pending samples metric when new shards start\n   - No accounting for samples that may still be flushing from old shards\n\n2. **Flush Timeout Handling (queue_manager.go:1286-1294):**\n   ```go\n   select {\n   case <-s.done:\n       return\n   case <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n   }\n   // Force an unclean shutdown\n   s.hardShutdown()\n   <-s.done\n   ```\n   - If flush times out, hard shutdown is initiated\n   - Pending samples are counted as dropped, but metric was already reset\n\n3. **Sample Enqueue with Metric Tracking (queue_manager.go:1312-1340):**\n   ```go\n   func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n       s.mtx.RLock()\n       defer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n\n       shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n       select {\n       case <-s.softShutdown:\n           return false\n       default:\n           appended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n           if !appended {\n               return false\n           }\n           ...\n           s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()  // Incremented here\n           ...\n       }\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Metrics Update After Send (queue_manager.go:1661-1695):**\n   - `updateMetrics()` decrements pending samples when batches are sent\n   - Called from `sendSamples()` which is called from each shard's `runShard()` goroutine\n   - This is the only place where pending samples are decremented\n\n5. **Recent Enhancements (CHANGELOG.md:292):**\n   - Issue #14450 added check to skip resharding if no successful send in past update period\n   - But this doesn't address the metric reset race during actual resharding\n\n### Test Case Evidence (queue_manager_test.go:514-550):\n- `TestReshard()` explicitly tests resharding but only verifies data eventually arrives\n- Does not stress-test the metric consistency during resharding\n- Does not test the flushDeadline timeout scenario\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **storage/remote/queue_manager.go**\n   - `reshardLoop()` - initiates resharding\n   - `start()` - creates new shards and resets metrics (BUG LOCATION)\n   - `stop()` - flushes old shards\n   - `enqueue()` - adds samples and increments metrics\n   - `updateMetrics()` - sends/drops samples and updates metrics\n\n2. **Metrics System:**\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - becomes inconsistent\n   - Other pending metrics (`pending_exemplars`, `pending_histograms`) - same issue\n\n3. **WAL and Target Discovery:**\n   - Target discovery changes trigger resharding\n   - New samples arrive while resharding is in progress\n   - Can cause contention between old/new shard queue assignments\n\n## Why This Is Intermittent\n\nThe issue is intermittent because it requires a specific timing window:\n\n1. **Trigger Condition:** Resharding must occur (usually due to load changes from target discovery updates)\n\n2. **Race Window:** The timing window exists between:\n   - When `stop()` begins its flushDeadline timeout\n   - When `start()` completes and resets the metric\n\n3. **Manifestation Depends On:**\n   - How many samples are pending when resharding occurs\n   - Whether the flush completes before the deadline\n   - Whether new samples arrive during the resharding window\n   - Which shard receives the stuck samples (random distribution based on series refs)\n\n4. **Why Not Always Visible:**\n   - If resharding happens when queue is empty, no samples to lose track of\n   - If resharding completes quickly (good network, small backlog), flush completes before timeout\n   - If samples resume flowing, the metric can eventually reconcile (though via error paths)\n\n## Diagnostic Approach\n\nTo confirm this root cause, monitor these metrics and logs simultaneously:\n\n1. **Logs to Watch:**\n   ```\n   \"level=info msg=\"Resharding queues\" from=X to=Y\"\n   \"level=info msg=\"Resharding done\" numShards=Y\"\n   ```\n\n2. **Metrics to Check:**\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - should increase when samples enqueued, decrease when sent\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_dropped_total{reason=\"...\"}` - count of dropped samples\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_shards` - number of active shards\n\n3. **Correlation Pattern:**\n   - Around resharding events, look for:\n     - `pending_samples` jumping to non-zero after resharding\n     - Some shards remaining idle (not processing any batches)\n     - Matching increase in `samples_dropped_total` immediately after the flush timeout\n\n4. **Network/Load Conditions:**\n   - Issue is most likely when:\n     - Remote endpoint is slow or temporarily unresponsive\n     - `flushDeadline` is exceeded during resharding\n     - High cardinality of series causes many shards to be involved\n\n## Recommendation\n\nThe fix requires ensuring metrics accurately reflect pending samples across resharding operations:\n\n### Fix Strategy (Priority Order):\n\n1. **Immediate:** Count pending samples from old shards BEFORE resetting metric\n   - Before `start()` resets the metric, query `enqueuedSamples` from each old shard\n   - Add those to a temporary counter\n   - Subtract as they're actually sent from old shards after resharding\n   - Initialize new shard metric to this value instead of 0\n\n2. **Alternative:** Defer metric reset until old shards confirm complete flush\n   - Modify `start()` to only reset metrics after receiving confirmation from old shards\n   - Or track metrics per-shard cohort (old vs. new) during resharding window\n\n3. **Robustness:** Increase `flushDeadline` or add exponential backoff\n   - Current timeout may be too short under load\n   - Consider longer deadline or retry logic before hard shutdown\n\n4. **Observability:** Add metrics for resharding events\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_resharding_duration_seconds` - time spent in resharding\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_flushed_during_reshard_total` - track samples during reshard\n   - Log samples lost due to hard shutdown with shard identifiers\n\n### Verification Steps:\n\nAfter fix is implemented, run:\n- Existing `TestReshard()` and `TestReshardRaceWithStop()` test cases\n- New stress test: trigger resharding while sending high-volume samples\n- New test: simulate `flushDeadline` timeout and verify metrics remain consistent\n- Integration test: verify metric consistency across upgrade with target discovery changes\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":4,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3504,"cache_read_input_tokens":77228,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3504},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"05b4cb1e-cd47-41db-b76a-e423a74f2a06","uuid":"b8c802ec-143a-403a-b293-33a3a7aa7695"}

The root cause is a race condition in the queue resharding mechanism where the pending samples metric (`prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending`) is reset to zero while samples may still be in flight, causing the metric to become inconsistent with actual pending data and creating stuck shards.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, functions `start()` (line 1241), `enqueue()` (lines 1312-1340), and the interaction between `reshardLoop()` (lines 1184-1199) and `updateMetrics()` (lines 1661-1695)\n\n**Mechanism:** The race condition involves an unsynchronized reset of the pending samples metric during resharding:\n\n1. **Metric Reset During Resharding** (line 1241 in `start()`):\n   ```go\n   func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n       s.mtx.Lock()\n       defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n\n       s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // <-- METRIC RESET\n       s.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n\n       newQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n       for i := range n {\n           newQueues[i] = newQueue(...)\n       }\n       s.queues = newQueues  // <-- Queue array replaced\n       ...\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Premature Metric Reset Timing:**\n   - When `reshardLoop()` calls `stop()`, old queue goroutines begin flushing samples\n   - `stop()` waits up to `flushDeadline` for samples to be sent (default varies, can be seconds)\n   - However, `start()` is called **immediately after** `stop()` returns\n   - `start()` unconditionally resets `pendingSamples` to 0 **before** verifying all pending samples were actually sent\n\n3. **Sample Flush Race Window:**\n   ```go\n   func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n       for {\n           select {\n           case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n               t.shards.stop()        // Tries to flush old shards\n               t.shards.start(numShards) // <-- IMMEDIATELY resets metrics\n           case <-t.quit:\n               return\n           }\n       }\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Incomplete Flush Scenario:**\n   - If `stop()` doesn't fully flush all samples within `flushDeadline`, it performs a hard shutdown\n   - Hard shutdown causes remaining samples to be dropped from the old shards\n   - But `start()` has already reset the metric, losing track of how many samples were dropped\n   - New samples enqueued to new shards are now tracked, but the metric started at 0 instead of reflecting the true pending count\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References:\n\n1. **Metrics Reset (queue_manager.go:1241):**\n   - Unconditional `Set(0)` on pending samples metric when new shards start\n   - No accounting for samples that may still be flushing from old shards\n\n2. **Flush Timeout Handling (queue_manager.go:1286-1294):**\n   ```go\n   select {\n   case <-s.done:\n       return\n   case <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n   }\n   // Force an unclean shutdown\n   s.hardShutdown()\n   <-s.done\n   ```\n   - If flush times out, hard shutdown is initiated\n   - Pending samples are counted as dropped, but metric was already reset\n\n3. **Sample Enqueue with Metric Tracking (queue_manager.go:1312-1340):**\n   ```go\n   func (s *shards) enqueue(ref chunks.HeadSeriesRef, data timeSeries) bool {\n       s.mtx.RLock()\n       defer s.mtx.RUnlock()\n\n       shard := uint64(ref) % uint64(len(s.queues))\n       select {\n       case <-s.softShutdown:\n           return false\n       default:\n           appended := s.queues[shard].Append(data)\n           if !appended {\n               return false\n           }\n           ...\n           s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Inc()  // Incremented here\n           ...\n       }\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Metrics Update After Send (queue_manager.go:1661-1695):**\n   - `reshardLoop()` - initiates resharding\n   - `start()` - creates new shards and resets metrics (BUG LOCATION)\n   - `stop()` - flushes old shards\n   - `enqueue()` - adds samples and increments metrics\n   - `updateMetrics()` - sends/drops samples and updates metrics\n\n2. **Metrics System:**\n   - `prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending` - becomes inconsistent\n   - Other pending metrics (`pending_exemplars`, `pending_histograms`) - The root cause is a race condition in the queue resharding mechanism where the pending samples metric (`prometheus_remote_storage_samples_pending`) is reset to zero while samples may still be in flight, causing the metric to become inconsistent with actual pending data and creating stuck shards.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Location:** `storage/remote/queue_manager.go`, functions `start()` (line 1241), `enqueue()` (lines 1312-1340), and the interaction between `reshardLoop()` (lines 1184-1199) and `updateMetrics()` (lines 1661-1695)\n\n**Mechanism:** The race condition involves an unsynchronized reset of the pending samples metric during resharding:\n\n1. **Metric Reset During Resharding** (line 1241 in `start()`):\n   ```go\n   func (s *shards) start(n int) {\n       s.mtx.Lock()\n       defer s.mtx.Unlock()\n\n       s.qm.metrics.pendingSamples.Set(0)  // <-- METRIC RESET\n       s.qm.metrics.numShards.Set(float64(n))\n\n       newQueues := make([]*queue, n)\n       for i := range n {\n           newQueues[i] = newQueue(...)\n       }\n       s.queues = newQueues  // <-- Queue array replaced\n       ...\n   }\n   ```\n\n2. **Premature Metric Reset Timing:**\n   - When `reshardLoop()` calls `stop()`, old queue goroutines begin flushing samples\n   - `stop()` waits up to `flushDeadline` for samples to be sent (default varies, can be seconds)\n   - However, `start()` is called **immediately after** `stop()` returns\n   - `start()` unconditionally resets `pendingSamples` to 0 **before** verifying all pending samples were actually sent\n\n3. **Sample Flush Race Window:**\n   ```go\n   func (t *QueueManager) reshardLoop() {\n       for {\n           select {\n           case numShards := <-t.reshardChan:\n               t.shards.stop()        // Tries to flush old shards\n               t.shards.start(numShards) // <-- IMMEDIATELY resets metrics\n           case <-t.quit:\n               return\n           }\n       }\n   }\n   ```\n\n4. **Incomplete Flush Scenario:**\n   - If `stop()` doesn't fully flush all samples within `flushDeadline`, it performs a hard shutdown\n   - Hard shutdown causes remaining samples to be dropped from the old shards\n   - But `start()` has already reset the metric, losing track of how many samples were dropped\n   - New samples enqueued to new shards are now tracked, but the metric started at 0 instead of reflecting the true pending count\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References:\n\n1. **Metrics Reset (queue_manager.go:1241):**\n   - Unconditional `Set(0)` on pending samples metric when new shards start\n   - No accounting for samples that may still be flushing from old shards\n\n2. **Flush Timeout Handling (queue_manager.go:1286-1294):**\n   ```go\n   select {\n   case <-s.done:\n       return\n   case <-time.After(s.qm.flushDeadline):\n   }\n   // Force an unclean shutdown\n   s.hardShutdown()\n   <-s.done\n   ```\n   -
